## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration (dA/dt) as a function of time and concentration, which is the fundamental problem of chemical reaction kinetics — determining the rate law. The presence of both t and A suggests possible explicit time dependence beyond simple power-law rate expressions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate expression)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (power-law with constant source/sink)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Photolysis with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (first-order with time-dependent forcing)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal-like kinetics)
- Competitive inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Combined mechanism: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 / (c1 + A) (mixed-order mechanism)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Integer reaction orders (1, 2, 3) correspond to elementary reaction steps; non-integer orders suggest complex mechanisms or fractal kinetics
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not t, the system is autonomous and follows a simple rate law — explicit t dependence indicates external forcing or non-isothermal conditions
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(c+A)) arise from quasi-steady-state approximations of multi-step mechanisms like enzyme kinetics
- Quadratic terms in A (A² or A*(c-A)) suggest bimolecular steps or autocatalytic reactions where the product catalyzes its own formation
- A rate expression with both positive and negative terms (e.g., c0*A - c1*A²) indicates competing forward and reverse or parallel reactions
- Fractional powers of time (t**c) in rate expressions suggest diffusion-limited reactions or reactions in heterogeneous/fractal media
- Exponential dependence on time often reflects Arrhenius-type temperature programming: k(t) = k0*exp(Ea*t) under linear temperature ramps
- If the rate law has the form c0*A*(c1-A), the system exhibits logistic behavior with a carrying capacity, common in autocatalysis
